Then, the Foreign Affairs Support Association's constitution and the original text of the telegram were passed. The following is an excerpt:

Convention Telegrams (A) "Telegraph to the Central Party Department, National Government, Executive Yuan, and Ministry of Foreign Affairs to cancel the China-Netherlands Consular Treaty." To the Central Party Department, National Government, and Executive Yuan, the China-Netherlands Consular Treaty was signed during the late Qing Dynasty, humiliating the country and selling out overseas Chinese. It should have been abolished long ago. In the past, bureaucratic diplomacy repeatedly missed opportunities. Our Premier was saddened by the national crisis and concerned about the difficulties of overseas Chinese. In his deathbed will, he paid special attention to "abolishing unequal treaties." If the Premier were still alive, this treaty would have been abolished long ago. It is found that the treaty was signed on May 8th of the Xuantong Year and approved for mutual exchange on July 28th of the same year. According to the provisions of Article 17 of the treaty, it should be implemented four months after the approval of the mutual exchange, that is, from November 28th of the same year. The treaty is valid for five years. When the term is about to expire, one of the two parties must notify at least one year in advance if it wants to stop the effect of the treaty. Counting from the mutual exchange of the treaty to the present, there have been four opportunities to "notify the cessation," namely in the Republic of China years 4, 9, 14, and this year. But at the latest, it must not be later than November 28th of this year. If it passes this day, it will have to be extended for another five years. At this critical moment, we earnestly hope that you will make a decisive decision and approve the immediate order to the Ministry of Foreign Affairs to immediately telegraph the Dutch side to abolish the "China-Netherlands Consular Treaty in Dutch Territories" and its annexes signed in 1911, redeem "the sale of overseas Chinese," and expand consular jurisdiction. Not only will the three million overseas Chinese compatriots in Dutch territories sing your praises, but our Premier in heaven will also smile happily. The timing is urgent and fleeting. If you approve, it will be fortunate for the Party and the country. Shanghai All Circles Support Xiao and Anti-Dutch Convention, Koutou, You. (B) Telegraph the Central Party Department, National Government, Executive Yuan, and Ministry of Foreign Affairs to negotiate and amend Article 109 of the Dutch Regulations. To the Central Party Department, National Government, and Executive Yuan, the Dutch government governs the Dutch territories based on the Dutch Regulations. Article 109 of the regulations stipulates that Japanese are assimilated to Europeans, and Chinese, Africans, Arabs, Muslims, and polytheists are assimilated to native aborigines. The Dutch have special harsh laws for governing native aborigines, so Chinese are also subject to these harsh laws. If we want to solve the suffering of overseas Chinese, instead of dealing with trivial details and treating the symptoms, it is better to grasp the key and make the greatest determination to negotiate with the Dutch government to amend Article 109 of the regulations, recognizing that Chinese are equal to Japanese and Europeans. At the same time, inform the Dutch side to cancel the "China-Netherlands Consular Treaty in Dutch Territories" and its annexes signed in 1911 and re-sign an equal consular treaty, then all difficulties will be solved easily. Your government and the council care for overseas Chinese, and all overseas Chinese rely on you. We earnestly request that you order the Ministry of Foreign Affairs to immediately request the Dutch government to amend Article 109 of the Dutch Regulations, the unequal provision of "Chinese being assimilated to native aborigines." We will not stop until we achieve our goal. We urgently present our case and await your orders with trepidation. Shanghai All Circles Support Xiao and Anti-Dutch Convention, Koutou, You. (C) "Ministry of Foreign Affairs, please negotiate to revoke the Dutch parliament's resolution to increase the head tax on entry." To the Ministry of Foreign Affairs in Nanjing, the Dutch colonial parliament resolved that from 1931, the immigration head tax will be increased again to 150 guilders per person. The Overseas Chinese Federation has telegraphed three times, requesting negotiations for revocation, but there has been no effect so far. The implementation period is only thirty days away. If we do not act quickly, how can we comfort the hopes of all overseas Chinese? For this reason, we appeal to your ministry to immediately telegraph the competent consul to make efforts to achieve the goal of revoking the case. Please also negotiate the case of collecting a head tax of 75 guilders for contracted Chinese workers upon entry and revoke it at the same time. If the Dutch side does not accept it, our anti-Dutch movement will not stop. In order to strive for equality between the two sides, we should ask your ministry to quickly submit it to the Executive Yuan and transfer it to the Legislative Yuan for deliberation and approval of the "Regulations on Collecting Head Tax on Dutch Overseas Chinese" to encourage and punish them. We are in urgent need of telegrams and await your orders with trepidation. Shanghai All Circles Support Xiao and Anti-Dutch Convention, Koutou, You. (D) "Telegraph the Ministry of Foreign Affairs to negotiate with the Dutch government to cancel the procedures for inspecting the passports of overseas Chinese entering the country and to automatically revoke the Provisional Passport Law." To the Ministry of Foreign Affairs, our overseas Chinese compatriots going to the Dutch territories have always enjoyed the same "passport exemption" treatment as Japan and Switzerland. Recently, the Dutch government has increasingly despised our China and stipulated that "Chinese entering the country will be refused to issue a residence permit if they do not hold a passport issued by their own government or its competent authority, stating that they are allowed to go to the Dutch East Indies, and the passport has been visaed by the competent Dutch consul." Obviously, our country is being treated differently from Japan and Switzerland. The Ministry of Foreign Affairs does not strive for it, which has disappointed the wishes of the people. Furthermore, it takes advantage of the opportunity and privately makes a provisional passport law to cater to the intentions of the Dutch, which is contrary to the purpose of our Premier's commitment to the revolution. We urgently request you to immediately revoke the provisional passport law and immediately order the competent envoys and consuls to negotiate with the Dutch government to cancel the procedures for inspecting the passports of overseas Chinese entering the country and to give them the same treatment as Japan and Switzerland. We are grateful. Shanghai All Circles Support Xiao and Anti-Dutch Convention, Koutou, You. (E) "Telegraph the Ministry of Foreign Affairs to question the reasons for stopping the boycott of Java ships." To Foreign Minister Wang in Nanjing, the Xiao case has occurred, and the whole country is indignant. The boycott of the Java movement in Xiamen is very fierce. However, the local garrison command went against public opinion and interfered arbitrarily. After our association telegraphed to question, we replied that we were handling it in accordance with your ministry's order. What is the intention? Please give a clear reply. Nanyang British and Dutch Territories Expelled Overseas Chinese Promotion National Diplomacy Support Association, Koutou, You. (F) (Omitted). (G) "Telegraph the whole country to assist the expelled overseas Chinese." To all newspapers, institutions, and compatriots in the country, our association members have personally suffered from the destruction and oppression of British and Dutch imperialism and have been expelled back to China. We mourn the decline of the nation and lament the plight of overseas Chinese compatriots. We hope that the whole country will unite to assist in order to carry out national diplomacy, overthrow imperialism, abolish unequal treaties, and relieve the suffering of overseas Chinese. Nanyang British and Dutch Territories Expelled Overseas Chinese Promotion National Diplomacy Support Association, Koutou, You.

Constitution of the Support Association Constitution of the China Republic Support Netherlands Foreign Affairs Association Article 1. This association is jointly organized by all circles of the Republic of China and aims solely at assisting the government in its negotiations with the Netherlands. It is named "China Republic Support Netherlands Foreign Affairs Association." Article 2. For the convenience of communication, the general assembly of this association is located in Shanghai, and branch offices may be established in relevant ministries, commissions, and commercial ports. Article 3. This association shall have fifty-one executive committee members and twenty-one supervisory committee members, who shall be elected by the general assembly of all circles. Article 4. This association shall have five standing committee members, who shall be mutually elected by the executive committee members. Article 5. When the standing committee, the executive committee, or individual standing committee members violate the law, the supervisory committee may submit an impeachment case, but it must be signed by more than half of the members. Article 6. The standing committee shall meet once every half month, the executive committee shall meet once a month, and the supervisory committee shall meet once every two months. In case of special circumstances, a temporary meeting may be convened. Article 7. All compatriots at home and abroad may make suggestions to this association regarding foreign affairs issues with the Netherlands. Article 8. The executive and supervisory committees must have more than one-third of the members present, and the standing committee must have more than half of the members present to hold a meeting. All proposals must be approved by more than half of the members to be resolved. If the number of votes is the same, the chairman shall decide. Article 9. If two meetings do not have the legal number of members present, a provisional resolution may be made, and the opinions of the absent members shall be sought to sign and decide whether to approve it. If the majority approves it, the provisional resolution may be implemented. Article 10. This association temporarily borrows a certain place as its office. Article 11. This association shall automatically dissolve after the victory of foreign affairs with the Netherlands. Article 12. If there are any matters not covered in this constitution, they may be amended by a joint meeting of the executive and supervisory committees. Article 13. This constitution shall be implemented after being passed by the general assembly of all circles.

Madam Zhang, Yu Fengzhi, Returned to Beijing Last Night

Zhang Xueming and Others Left Shanghai in the Same Train

All Circles Expressed Deep Gratitude for the Hospitality

Song Ziwen and Song Ziliang Also Traveled Together

Madam Yu Fengzhi, wife of Deputy Commander Zhang, and her entourage took a special train back to Beijing at 11 PM last night. Zhang Xueming and his wife, Hu Ruoyu, Mr. and Mrs. Shen Zutong, Mr. and Mrs. Wu Jingan, Gao Jiyi, Zhang Yujiu, adjutants, and guards also accompanied them. The following is a record of yesterday's activities and the situation at the station:

Tea Party at Wu's Residence Yesterday at noon, Xiong Shihui and Mr. and Mrs. Kong Xiangxi sent invitations to Yu Fengzhi and others for lunch. At 4 PM, Mr. and Mrs. Wu Tiecheng held a tea party at their private residence on Haige Road to welcome them. Zhang Xueming, Hu Ruoyu, Zhang Yujiu, and other leaders of various agencies attended. Yu declined due to physical fatigue. The party ended at around 5 PM. At 7 PM last night, Finance Minister Song Ziwen and his wife specially hosted a banquet at their private residence. Madam Zhang and others rushed to attend one after another. At around 8 PM, the guests and hosts dispersed happily.

Banquet at Du's Residence At 8 PM last night, Wu Tiecheng, Yang Yunshi, Liu Zhilu, Yang Xiaotian, Wang Xiaolai, Huang Jinrong, Zhang Xiaolin, Du Yuesheng, and others hosted a banquet at Du's residence on Huage Road, inviting Zhang Qun, Xiong Shihui, Du Xigui, Gu Weijun, Liu Jiwen, Jiang Dingwen, Li Mingyang, Wang Boling, Xu Weizhen, Yang Zhonghu, Song Ziliang, and other dignitaries from various agencies and circles to accompany them. The French consul also attended. Northeast dignitaries attending included Gao Jiyi, Zhang Yujiu, Hu Ruoyu, Mr. and Mrs. Shen Zutong, Mr. and Mrs. Shen Nengyi, and Qian Xumi. Zhang Xueming and others arrived first after the banquet at the Song's residence. Madam Zhang also arrived and was warmly entertained by Mr. and Mrs. Zhang Xiaolin and Mr. and Mrs. Du Yuesheng. That night, there was also a famous opera performance. Yang Shaolou arrived in Shanghai from Beijing at 10 PM last night and went to Du's residence. Due to fatigue from the journey, he did not perform on stage. At 10:30 PM, Madam Zhang and her party bid farewell and were personally escorted to the station by Du and others.

Station Arrangement Madam Zhang was originally scheduled to leave Shanghai at 8 AM yesterday due to Deputy Commander Zhang's telegram summoning her back to Beijing. Minister Song telegraphed the Railway Bureau to prepare a special train. Later, due to other social engagements, it was changed to 8 PM that night, and then to 11 PM. After receiving the news, the Railway Bureau immediately prepared a special train consisting of one flower car No. 511, one first-class sleeping car, one first-class dining car, and one luggage car and parked it on Platform No. 4 to await orders. Later, Minister of Finance Song Ziwen also happened to be returning to Beijing, so Minister Song's flower car was also added. The highest-speed connecting car, G No. 20, was used to tow it. It departed from the North Station at exactly 11 PM last night and did not stop along the way. It is expected to arrive in the capital at 6 AM this morning. The Railway Bureau specially assigned Chen Xinghan, the section chief of the two-way resident office, to preside over the affairs of the entire train, and the night shift section chiefs along the way assisted. All hospitality matters were handled by receptionist Zhou Zhangwu. The night express train departed afterward. From the gate to the special train, soldiers from the 1st Regiment of the Capital Garrison, a company of soldiers from the 27th Regiment of the 5th Division, and the 3rd Detachment of the Municipal Public Security Bureau were fully armed to guard. On the platform, there was also a military band from the Garrison Command and the Municipal Public Security Bureau to see them off. Madam Zhang's flower car was filled with dozens of flower baskets and other gifts from all circles. All the luggage was transported to the station by followers at around 11 AM yesterday and loaded into the luggage car.

Farewell Party Madam Zhang and others arrived at the North Station at 10:40 PM. Those who came to the station to see them off included Mayor Zhang and his wife, Mr. and Mrs. Wu Tiecheng, Mr. and Mrs. Sheng En颐, Madam Tang Shaoyi, Zheng Yuxiu, Mr. and Mrs. Du Yuesheng, Zhang Xiaolin, Mr. and Mrs. Shen Nengyi, Qian Jiechen, Liu Yunfang, and dozens of others. At 11 PM, Song Ziwen, Song Zi'an, and Song Ziliang arrived at the station and boarded the flower car to chat with Madam Zhang briefly. With a whistle, the special train slowly moved, and the military music played in unison. Madam Zhang also leaned out the window and nodded goodbye to the farewell party, repeatedly saying that she was very grateful for the special hospitality of everyone.

Zhang's Trip to the North Our reporter inquired about Deputy Commander Zhang's trip to the north from a Northeast dignitary yesterday. Zhang was originally scheduled to attend the State Council meeting on the 28th and then take the Jinpu train north. Now, because he still has important matters to discuss with Chairman Jiang, he will not be able to leave until the 29th.

Wenzhou Rejection of Donations Case Yesterday Again Stirred Up Waves

Resolution Overturned Again

Department Stores Stopped Shipping to Shanghai

The various merchant guilds of Wenzhou, due to the Yongjia Unified Donation Bureau changing the tax collection method for foreign and domestic goods to a unified donation system, raised objections, implemented a strike of shipping and tax payment suspension, lasting for ten days. On the 25th, it was initially mediated by the Chamber of Commerce, and the tax bureau also agreed to revert to the old regulations, and the turmoil subsided. This matter was reported in yesterday's newspaper. Unexpectedly, yesterday, on the first day of the Wenzhou merchant guilds resuming tax payment and cargo transportation, just as they were reporting the loading, the tax bureau suddenly created another complication, causing the already calmed turmoil to suddenly stir up a huge and malicious wave again. Yesterday, the reporter went to various parties to inquire. According to the urgent telegrams sent from Wenzhou yesterday afternoon received by various shipping companies in this port, all stated that since the mediation and resolution of the donation rejection turmoil on the 25th, it was originally planned to load goods and resume transportation as usual today. Unexpectedly, the donation bureau overturned the case, causing the already agreed upon resolution to be completely overturned. The Wenzhou business community is extremely indignant about this. All industries have continued to reject donations and suspend transportation from today (the 27th), and the situation is dangerous, even worse than before. This matter between the two parties has gradually deteriorated, each tending towards extremes. The China Merchants Steam Navigation Company also received a telegram from the Wenzhou branch, vaguely stating that the donation turmoil has been overturned, and department stores have stopped again. The "Guangji" steamer was originally scheduled to sail to Shanghai on the 26th, and had already secured cargo for Shanghai, and was about to load it onto the ship. Unexpectedly, an unexpected event occurred, and the cargo was temporarily withdrawn by the customers. It had to go to Shanghai empty, temporarily buying mud and sand as ballast. The telegram was brief, not stating the unexpected change in detail, but the situation is very dangerous.

The "Jingshan Maru" Collision with "Xinfeng" Case: Responsibility for the Accident

Evidence is Clear, Will Request Public Judgment

If Not Satisfied, Will File a Maritime Lawsuit

The China Merchants Steam Navigation Company's "Xinfeng" steamer was damaged by the Japanese ship "Jingshan Maru" at Yangzhuangzi, Tanggu, Tianjin, and was brought to Shanghai for major repairs. The losses of goods and the ship's hull amounted to more than 40,000 yuan. The company negotiated with the Japanese postal service and coastal shipping company, demanding compensation, which was reported in this newspaper earlier. It is now learned that the Japanese have rejected this matter and do not admit their mistake. The information obtained is recorded below.

Responsibility for the Accident is Clear: Investigating the "Jingshan Maru" collision with the "Xinfeng" steamer, it was because the Japanese ship did not comply with maritime regulations, going upstream to exit the port. According to the regulations, the downstream ship entering the port should yield. At that time, the "Xinfeng" steamer was sailing into Zizhulin with the downstream tide. Because the regulations require oncoming ships to give way, it hung a green light at the bow. Unexpectedly, the "Jingshan Maru" violated navigation rules, causing the "Xinfeng" to be crushed and suffered huge losses. The shipowner, Ma Xun, feared that the Japanese would be cunning and try to evade responsibility. In addition to negotiating with the shipowner of the "Jingshan Maru" on the spot and obtaining a certificate from the Japanese admitting their mistake, he also reported to the Tianjin Customs and requested the River Shipping Department to inspect the ship, proving that the responsibility lay with the Japanese. Therefore, the "Xinfeng"'s reasons for claiming compensation are very sufficient.

The Japanese Refused to Compensate: The China Merchants Steam Navigation Company, based on the report of the shipowner, Ma Xun, and the Japanese ship captain's admission of responsibility for the collision, and totaled more than 40,000 yuan for the damaged goods and ship's hull, issued a list, and sent a letter from the company to the Tianjin branch of the Japanese Postal Service's Coastal Shipping Department, demanding compensation for the losses. After this letter was sent, it was heard yesterday that the Tianjin Japanese Postal Service had replied to Shanghai, refusing to admit the responsibility of the "Jingshan Maru" for the accident, and also refusing to pay for the damage and repair costs of the "Xinfeng" freighter. The tone of the letter seemed to shift the responsibility for the collision to the "Xinfeng," but only expressed regret for the collision of the two ships, cunningly denying compensation and not admitting their mistake.

This Case Will Be Submitted to Arbitration: The China Merchants Steam Navigation Company received the Japanese reply denying responsibility. It is heard that the steps to deal with it have been discussed. Since the responsibility for this case is clear and cannot be evaded, the Japanese shipowner has a handwritten certificate of the accident, and the Tianjin Customs and River Shipping Department have also inspected the ship and stated that the responsibility lies with the Japanese ship. Therefore, the company intends to submit the case to the Tianjin Customs for public judgment. Since the accident occurred in Tianjin, and the public witness is the Tianjin Customs and River Shipping Department, it can make the Japanese convinced and unable to use their cunning tricks again. In case of dissatisfaction with the public judgment, a maritime lawsuit will be filed.

Guangdong People's Four Organizations Welcomed Chen Mingshu the Day Before Yesterday

Chen Had an Important Speech

At 4 p.m. on the 25th, the Shanghai Guangzhao Public Association, the Guangdong Overseas Chinese Business Federation, the Huzhou Guild Hall, and the Zhongshan Fellow Villagers Association held a meeting at the Guangdong Business Federation to welcome Guangdong Provincial Government Chairman Chen Zhenru, Railway Minister Sun Zhesheng, and Jianghai Customs Superintendent Liu Jiwen. Hundreds of people attended the meeting. Tang Shaochuan was elected chairman and Li Zhuoying recorded the proceedings. After the ceremony, Chairman Tang delivered a welcome speech, vaguely stating that today the fellow villagers welcome Chairman Chen, welcoming his determination to build various undertakings in Guangdong, and Minister Sun and Superintendent Liu also have the goal of increasing the welfare of our people. The fellow villagers present should all stand up and pay their respects. The people of Guangdong have always possessed a spirit of creation and determination to build. The revolution also originated in Guangdong. Wherever the people of Guangdong go, they have established great public welfare and charitable undertakings. For example, Mr. Chen Bingqian, the chairman of the Guangdong Overseas Chinese Business Federation, donates huge sums of money annually in Shanghai to run the Guangdong Business Hospital, with remarkable results. The new Guangzhao Zhuang land base of more than 300 mu requires tens of thousands of yuan, and it also relies on Mr. Bingqian's strong leadership to complete this good deed. This shows that the people of Guangdong are courageous in running local public welfare undertakings. Since the revolution, the people of Guangdong have borne the heaviest burden and made the greatest sacrifices. Moreover, due to years of war, the provincial treasury's income has been mostly used for military expenses, not giving the people of Guangdong the opportunity to realize the ideals of the era of the late Premier Sun. As far as I know, for two years, the annual income of the provincial treasury reached 100 million yuan, but military expenses accounted for seven or eight tenths, so how could there be funds to seek construction? Fortunately, the war has subsided, and Chairman Chen has engaged in construction, which is truly a blessing for the people of Guangdong. Please Chairman Chen announce a thing or two about the construction of the Fozhong Railway and the Zhongshan Port plan, so that everyone can understand everything. After speaking, Chairman Chen Zhenru stood up and spoke, vaguely stating that he, Minister Sun, and Superintendent Liu are extremely grateful for the fellow villagers' organizations holding a meeting to welcome them today. As for the construction plans for Zhongshan Port and the Fozhong Railway, he and Minister Sun had already stated everything at the Apricot Blossom Building banquet with fellow villagers last night (the 24th). Now that the fellow villagers have gathered again, he should briefly state one or two things about the two plans. The construction of Zhongshan Port was initiated by Mr. Tang Shaochuan and proposed by Chen, and the recent Fourth Plenary Session approved the construction. Upon investigation, the port belongs to a sea mouth, and after measurement, the water depth is 25 feet, so even large ships can come and go. After expert research, it is considered a natural port. The port construction fee is designated to be allocated from the refunded Boxer Indemnity. The National Government has announced that the port is a free port. Some have doubted that the port is not a free port because the Customs Tax Department did not pay attention to setting up a customs office there. Later, Finance Minister Song discovered that there were smuggling and tax evasion malpractices there, so he explicitly ordered that the place was not a free port. But at this time, the National Government has ordered the Ministry of Finance to demarcate the boundary and set up a customs office within two months. This port is indeed a free port. This Zhongshan Port line is necessary for construction in terms of transportation and geographical advantages, so the construction of the railway on this line is even more urgent. It is now planned to build the Fozhong Railway, from Foshan in Guangdong to Zhongshan Port. The railway connects to the Guangzhou-Shaoguan section of the Guangdong-Hong Kong Railway, passing through Chencun, Daliang, Rongqi, Xiaolan, and Shiqi to reach Zhongshan Free Port. If funds are sufficient, a branch line from Xiaolan to Guzhen on the opposite bank of Jiangmen will also be built. The areas passed through are all known as rich areas in Guangdong Province, with rice and silk as the main products, which are exported in large quantities every year. In the future, when the railway is built, the business will be prosperous and can be guaranteed. The main line from Foshan to Zhongshan Port is about 66 miles long, and the construction cost is estimated to be more than 11.3 million yuan. The branch line from Xiaolan to Guzhen is about 7 miles long, and the construction cost is estimated to be more than 1.2 million yuan. The construction of the main and branch lines at the same time will cost about 12.57 million yuan, and it is estimated that it can be completed in at most two years. The construction plan has been formulated by the Ministry of Railways, and the Guangzhou-Shaoguan section of the Yuehan Railway has been ordered to send a team to survey and estimate. After the estimate is received, construction can be actively carried out. It is also planned to jointly organize an official-business joint venture company with merchants and the people, with the government and the merchants and the people each contributing 6.25 million yuan to achieve rapid results. Now that the war has ended, Guangdong Province has entered a period of construction. He should do his best to actively build the province to live up to the expectations of the fellow villagers. He has always had a sense of responsibility and shame, and always seeks to put things into practice. The interests of the people should be protected by law. He can announce this to the fellow villagers, alleviate the suffering of the merchants and the people, and hope that the fellow villagers will provide guidance at any time, etc. Sun Zhesheng (Minister Sun went to Nanjing for business and was represented by Counselor Liang Hancao), Zheng Yuxiu, and Chen Bingqian also gave speeches in succession. At 6 p.m., they dispersed in joy.

British Economic Investigation Group

Will Arrive in Shanghai at the End of the Month

The British Economic Investigation Group will arrive in Shanghai on November 30th on the British company's "Rawalpindi" steamer from Japan, or may arrive on the evening of the 29th, which is also uncertain. Its accommodation has been set at the Cathay Hotel. It is learned that the country's reception procedure in Shanghai is as follows: After arriving in the port, investigate the situation in Shanghai. On the afternoon of December 3rd, take a train to Beijing. On the 4th and 5th, they will be entertained by Chinese and British authorities in Beijing. Leave Beijing on the 6th, taking a train or a river boat, which has not yet been determined. On the 8th, attend a banquet at the Shanghai British Chamber of Commerce, located at the Shanghai Club. On the 9th, attend a banquet hosted by the Mayor of Shanghai. On the 10th, attend a formal welcome meeting at the Shanghai Municipal Social Affairs Bureau at noon. International Silver Commission Consultant Aitzla Arrives in Shanghai

Will Lend Huge Sums of Silver to China

The "North-China Daily News" reported that after the disastrous fall in silver prices, many leaders from the industrial and financial sectors and economists gathered in Washington to organize the International Silver Commission, and elected former US Senator Cameron as the chairman, planning to restore silver prices. In March of this year, Cameron advocated lending a huge sum of silver to China, amounting to about 500 million ounces, for construction purposes. The interest rate is not high, and after forty or fifty years, it will still be returned in silver. This silver will be minted into silver coins in Shanghai, and its use will be guided by a committee composed of seven representatives from the lending country and seven representatives from China. Now, the consultant of the commission, Mr. Aitzla, has arrived in Shanghai and is discussing the matter with leaders of overseas merchants and prominent bankers in this port. According to his words to the reporter of this newspaper, this loan must first obtain the consent of other relevant countries, but if China is prepared to accept it, it is expected that other countries will not object. If it is established, it will not only alleviate China's difficulties, but also immediately increase the world's silver prices, which will increase China's purchasing power for gold-using countries. Therefore, all countries will benefit, not just the United States alone. At present, China is worried about the danger of communism. This loan is enough to provide work for millions of workers, so that they can live and work in peace, so it can also potentially eliminate the crisis of communism, which is beneficial to world peace. As for its impact on silver prices, it can be proved by facts. The ratio of world gold and silver production has not changed from before. From 1493 to 1923, 13,215,290,481 ounces of silver and 924,599,182 ounces of gold were produced, a ratio of about 31 to 1. It is estimated that of this amount, there are still 7 billion ounces of silver and 500 million ounces of gold for currency use. If all of this gold and silver were minted into coins, then according to today's US ratio, gold is 20.67 cents per ounce and silver is 1.29 and 29/100 cents per ounce. The total value of the silver coins minted will not be as large as that of the gold coins. This shows that the production of silver is not excessive. It is only because countries are melting coins that silver prices have fallen drastically. At present, the world's annual silver production is about 255 million ounces, of which the United States produces about 60 million, Canada about 20 million, and Mexico about 100 million. In total, the Americas produce about 85% of the world's production. The world's annual gold production is about 20 million ounces, half of which is produced in South Africa.

News of the End of Military Transportation

Rent Paid in Full... Medals Awarded

The military transportation has ended, and the ships requisitioned by the Communications Office have been released one after another. They will all resume sailing soon. The situation after the end of the military transportation is described in detail below.

Ship Rent Paid: The ship rent for the ships requisitioned by the Communications Office was originally paid up to the end of September. In October and November, more than ten ships were rented again, all from the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company and the Sanbei Steamship Company. The rent payable has been settled by Yu Qiaqing and Li Zhonggong, who went to the capital to negotiate with the Communications Office Management Office. It has now been collected and returned to Shanghai by Yu and Li. The remaining amount will be paid in full soon after the ships are released (there are still five ships).

Reward for Crew Members: The commercial ships requisitioned this time have made contributions to the anti-rebel army, and some have made great achievements. Now that the military affairs have come to an end, the Communications Office has submitted a report to the headquarters, vaguely stating that the crew members of the commercial ships of various companies who were assigned to military transportation worked hard to transport and increased the efficiency of military affairs, which is deeply commendable. Now that the military affairs have been settled, the personnel who have made efforts should be investigated and rewarded to show encouragement. Now, regulations have been drafted, which have been approved by the Commander-in-Chief, as follows: Regulations for Rewarding Military Commercial Ships and Shipping Personnel, Article 1: In order to encourage military commercial ships and shipping personnel to serve diligently during the military period and increase the transportation capacity of the army, these regulations are specially formulated to reward them. Article 2: The rewarded personnel will be awarded a medal by the Headquarters of the Army, Navy, and Air Force for them to wear to show their achievements. Article 3: The medals are divided into two types, A and B. All staff members below the shipowner and shipping company personnel will be awarded type A medals, and those who serve outside of the staff will be awarded type B medals. The design of the medals and licenses is attached. Article 4: Regardless of whether they are staff members or not, they must have one of the following to be eligible to open a fact and apply for a reward: A. Those who risked passing through enemy fire and handled it properly; B. Those who have been harmed; C. Those who, under special circumstances, have properly handled it and relied on it to protect all public property; D. Those who have properly handled emergency situations with independent judgment; E. Those who have served on the ship for six months during the military transportation period without fault; F. Those who have suffered losses due to public affairs; G. Those who have been diligent and outstanding in handling military ships; H. Those who have assisted and been diligent and outstanding in handling matters during the military transportation period. Article 5: The award of medals shall be proposed by the Shipping Association or the company in accordance with the provisions of Articles 3 and 4 of these regulations, and the name list for applying for medals shall be filled out in accordance with the form and sent to the Traffic Office of the Headquarters by letter. After review and verification, it shall be submitted to the Commander-in-Chief for issuance. Article 6: These regulations shall be implemented from the date of approval. Yesterday, the various shipping companies in this port have followed orders to investigate and report the names of personnel who have made efforts to apply for awards.

Absolute Severance Measures Will Be Taken

Trademark for "4711" Cologne

No One Can Imitate

The "4711" cologne managed by the Mei Zui Shi Foreign Firm is exclusively manufactured and distributed by the German Cologne-based Ferdinand Mülhens Company, and no one can imitate it. The distillation method is handed down from ancestors, so its trademark "4711" can only be used for the cologne of that company. According to a telegram from the United States, an American merchant named Meihang Guberfu had purchased the "4711" trademark from the Enemy Property Administration during the European War to manufacture cologne. After lengthy negotiations initiated by the German "4711" company, the Supreme Court of the United States recently ruled that the plaintiff has the exclusive right to use the "4711" trademark, and the trademark rights purchased by the defendant are revoked and invalid.

Page 11

Local News 2

Jiang Weiyu Escapes Danger

Claims to Have Escaped from a Bandit's Den...Using Opium and Wine as Clever Tactics

Another Account Says He Was Redeemed with Money...10,000 Silver Dollars

Jiang Weiyu, the owner of the Jiang Xiangxing butchery at 687 Jiaotong Road, Zhabei, was kidnapped at his doorstep at 6:30 PM on the 23rd of last month. The kidnappers sent a letter to Jiang's family demanding a ransom of 300,000 yuan. Jiang Weiyu's brother, Weibin, contacted the kidnappers using a "lost and found" advertisement in the newspaper, as detailed in this newspaper's issue of the 24th of this month. However, there was no further news after the hostage's brother placed the second advertisement. Until about 3:00 AM yesterday morning, Jiang Weiyu suddenly returned home and surrendered himself to the Taiyangmiao Police Station of the Fourth District Public Security Bureau in Zhabei, claiming that he had escaped from the bandit's den. The details of his escape are recorded below. However, according to another source, Jiang's escape was actually due to his redemption with 10,000 silver dollars.

Conditions in the Den: Jiang Weiyu arrived at the Taiyangmiao Police Station of the Fourth District Public Security Bureau at approximately 3:10 AM yesterday morning and described his escape, saying that after being kidnapped on the evening of the 23rd, he was blindfolded with black glasses in the bandits' car, so he was unaware of the conditions outside the car. After about an hour, he was taken out of the car by two bandits and walked for about five to six minutes before arriving at a house, where he was imprisoned. The place seemed very remote, without any sound of people or horses, only the faint sound of a steam whistle could be heard. Two guards, both speaking in the local dialect, ordered him to write a letter to his family demanding a ransom of 300,000 yuan. After four or five days, the bandits moved him to a small boat, and then he returned to land.

Opium and Wine as Clever Tactics: Jiang claimed that there were often ten to twenty people coming and going in the bandit's den, some wearing Western suits and some speaking Mandarin. Whenever there were negotiations or conversations, the bandits would cover their heads with masks to prevent being recognized. The bandit's den provided excellent hospitality and freedom of food and drink. After two or three weeks, Jiang suddenly came up with a plan to escape. He deceitfully told the bandits that life in the den was boring and that he was counting the days, hoping to be supplied with opium and wine for entertainment. After the guards obtained approval from their superiors, they provided him with rice wine with every meal and two or three opium pills in the evening when the sun was setting and the lights were not yet on, allowing Jiang to smoke them. Jiang deliberately acted pleased, pleading for two more pills the next day, and secretly offered them to the guards. These two guards were originally addicts, and they were extremely close to Jiang because of this unexpected gift, and Jiang often used leftover wine and food to hold festivities.

Escaped Late at Night: After several days of this, Jiang consumed opium and wine every day, with the amount of wine being even greater than the opium. On the night before last, at dinner time, Jiang deliberately left a large amount of wine for the guards to drink wildly. Around 11:00 PM, the bandits were completely drunk and curled up on the ground. Jiang saw that the opportunity had arrived, immediately got up, walked around the room, deliberately making noise. The bandits did not get up or ask questions, so he lit a match to illuminate the room and walked outside to urinate. When he returned, the bandits were still dead drunk, only muttering unintelligible words. At this point, Jiang became bold and pushed open the door. After passing through a courtyard, he opened another door and groped in the darkness to find a small path, supporting himself against the wall as he walked straight to the fields. After crossing a small ditch, he crossed a main road. Jiang immediately ran wildly without looking back. It was already midnight at that time. After running like this for an hour, he finally saw signs of people. He caught sight of a rickshaw coming towards him and jumped into the car, ordering the driver to pull him forward. After about a quarter of an hour, he suddenly arrived at the Tiantong'an, realizing that he was far away from the bandit's den and gradually approaching home, which greatly comforted him. Around 3:00 AM, Jiang returned home safely.

Another Account: The above is all that Jiang Weiyu told the police station himself. However, another source said that Jiang's escape was actually due to his redemption with 10,000 silver dollars. Because the hostage's brother, Weibin, placed an advertisement agreeing to a price of 15,000 yuan, the bandits were still not satisfied and sent three more letters to the hostage's side, arranging to meet at the New World Hotel. When the time came, a well-dressed person went there. The detectives in charge of this case followed him out, took the No. 5 tram from Daxin Street, and changed cars at the West Gate to Xiaonanmen. Unfortunately, they were noticed being followed and took the opportunity to escape. Afterwards, Jiang's family prepared the money and went to redeem him, so he was released. Although it is impossible to be certain whether this account is true, judging from the extent of the negotiations between the two sides, it may not be groundless, so it is recorded here for your reference.

Circumstances of the Kidnapping: On the 23rd of last month, Jiang Weiyu was driving his own delivery truck from the butchery to deliver goods to the distribution point on Kang Nao Tuo Road when he was kidnapped. There were five bandits in total, all armed with pistols. The truck was found on Ma Yushan Road the next morning, but Jiang was nowhere to be seen. He was presumed to be living in the bandit's den until yesterday morning, when he returned in a disheveled state. When he was kidnapped, he was wearing a green wool shirt and shorts. When he returned home yesterday, his clothes were the same as before, but he was haggard and exhausted.

Zhou Changshan Escapes from Bandit's Den Wounded

Kidnappers Chase and Shoot

Hostage Hit by Bullet, But Does Not Exit

Zhou Changshan, a Ningbo native, was kidnapped on the morning of the 16th of last month at Jiangwan Sports Association West Road. On the 9th of this month, the General Patrol Room of the Public Concession arrested a bandit named Wang in connection with another case, who confessed that the hostage Zhou Changshan was hidden in a thatched house on East Sports Stadium Road. Detectives and constables, led by the bandit, went to the Fifth Police Station of the Zhabei District. Director Dai led Inspector Wei and senior constables to the address for a search, but found nothing. Only two suspects, Yang Yunsheng and Xu Zhaoxiang, natives of Jiangwan, were arrested. After Director Dai interrogated the bandit Wang repeatedly, the bandit confessed that the hostage had been moved to 279 1/2 Pingliang Road, Yangshupu. Director Dai, upon receiving this information, led his officers to the address, but found no one there either. Therefore, the two suspects were handed over to the police station for further investigation. After two weeks, the hostage's whereabouts remain unknown. Around 4:00 PM on the afternoon of the 25th, Gao Yinguang, Jiao Fugui, and Yuan Guanyi, third-class constables from the Third Police Station of the Sixth District Public Security Bureau, were conducting a household census in the countryside when they passed by Zhangjiatang, about two li southeast of Caohejing. They saw a crowd of villagers gathered to watch something. Constables Gao and the others, not knowing what was happening, squeezed into the crowd and saw a man about 30 years old wearing a sanitary shirt and pants, barefoot and without shoes, with a gunshot wound on his right shoulder. When the officers inquired, the injured man was mentally confused and unable to speak. According to the villagers, five or six people from Qianliangmiao (in Shanghai County) were chasing the man and shot him for unknown reasons. The villagers said the chasers fled southeast. In addition to leaving one person to guard the injured man, the constables also tracked southeast for about a li, but did not see any trace of the bandits. As they were unarmed, they did not dare to pursue further and had to return to the station to report. After receiving the report, Director Liu immediately led his officers to the scene to investigate. Meanwhile, he sent Inspector Yuan and Patrol Captain Fu, along with constables, to search the southeast in different directions, all the way to the Huangpu River. However, as too much time had passed, they were unable to catch the bandits. They then ordered the constables to carry the injured man back to the station. At this time, the injured man was slightly more lucid. He identified himself as Zhou Changshan, a Ningbo native, 33 years old, a member of the Shanghai Concession Merchant Corps, residing at 27 Niuzhuang Road. He said he had been kidnapped on the morning of October 16th at Jiangwan Road and taken into a car with black glasses on, and ordered to hold a newspaper in front of his face as if he was reading, with two bandits watching him on either side, not allowing him to make a sound. The car drove for about half an hour, then transferred to a small boat, and landed in a village, where he was hidden in a secret room in the bandit's den, unable to take a step beyond it. Along the way, he wore black glasses and did not know the route. For the past forty days, he had been wearing shackles every day, and the surveillance was very strict, and the treatment was also very harsh. There were eight bandits in total, with five pistols. They had previously forced him to write a letter to his family demanding a ransom of 200,000 yuan. Apparently, his family had already paid 60,000 yuan. Recently, the bandits told him that his family had reported to the Des Voeux Road Police Station and that a large number of detectives would be coming to search soon, so the bandits were extremely panicked. This afternoon, he took the opportunity to climb over the earthen wall from the bandit's den and managed to escape. Later, the bandits noticed and chased after him. He only cared about escaping and did not distinguish the direction. After escaping for about four or five li, he was caught by the bandits, who shot at him. After being injured, he was still able to run a few steps, but then he fainted on the ground. The villagers heard the sound of gunfire and gathered together, and the bandits fled at that time. As for where the bandit's den was, he did not know. He requested to be sent to the Red Cross Hospital for treatment and to notify his family. Director Liu, considering the cold weather, lent Zhou Changshan clothes, shoes, and hats to wear, hired a car to send him to the Haig Road Red Cross Hospital for treatment. After examination by the doctor, it was found that Zhou Changshan had a gunshot wound about two inches below his right shoulder, the bullet did not exit, and his life was in great danger. In addition to ordering senior constables to conduct a thorough investigation to ensure that he was caught and brought to justice, he also prepared a written report on the rescue of Zhou Changshan, along with a medical certificate, and submitted it to the Municipal Public Security Bureau for review and action.

Tragic Car Accident Involving Westerners Results in Death and Injury

Peng Jieming's Life in Danger

Mrs. Shi's Life Also Hanging by a Thread

Russian Policeman Died Instantly

Martial Artist Escapes with Minor Injuries

At 2:30 AM yesterday, a tragic car accident involving Westerners occurred at the intersection of Route Lafayette and Route Albert in the French Concession, resulting in death and injury. The detailed report of the incident is as follows:

Two Cars Collide Violently: At 2:30 AM yesterday, in the middle of the night, an Englishwoman, Mrs. Scott, was returning from a dinner party at a friend's house, driving a blue convertible car with license plate number 7498. As she drove along Route Lafayette in the French Concession and approached the intersection of Route Albert, near pole number 65 at the corner of the Chinese-French National Industrial Vocational School, just as she was about to turn the steering wheel to turn from south to west, a Russian policeman named Popov, a horse patrolman with the French General Patrol Room, was driving a yellow car with license plate number 6480 from north to south. Both cars were traveling at full speed, and there was no time to avoid each other, resulting in a violent collision.

Each Suffers Severe Injuries: At the time, due to the excessive force of the collision, Mrs. Scott's car was launched onto the roadside, collapsing the short wall of the industrial school, which was more than a foot thick. Fragments of glass from the car flew more than fifteen feet away. Mrs. Scott and Mr. Peng, who was riding with her, were both seriously injured. Peng's skull was fractured, and he suffered severe injuries to his face and chest. Mrs. Scott was thrown out of the car, seven or eight feet away, and fell unconscious on the sidewalk. Her arms, legs, and face were all severely injured. Russian policeman Popov was also thrown out of the car, eight feet away, and lay unconscious in a pool of blood, still tightly gripping a broken piece of the steering wheel in his hand. His internal organs were severely injured, and he was bleeding profusely.

Death and Injury Alike: After the accident, nearby patrol officers immediately noticed and blew their whistles for help. A Western patrol officer from the Baojian Road Police Station, who was patrolling nearby, heard the sound and rushed to the scene. They immediately used cars to first send Mr. Peng Jieming to Guangci Hospital. As of last night, he was still unconscious and in danger of death. Mrs. Scott was sent to Hongen Hospital. After being treated by doctors, she temporarily regained consciousness, but her injuries were in critical areas and her condition was also very dangerous. Popov died before reaching the door of Guangci Hospital due to his severe injuries. As for Mr. Lucas, a Russian martial artist who was in the same car with Popov, although he also fell out of the car, he woke up after a few minutes and only suffered injuries to his wrists. He was bandaged by the doctor and then discharged from the hospital.

Background of Each Person: Yesterday, the French police first temporarily detained both cars and notified the General Transportation Department to send personnel to the scene of the accident to survey the truth of the accident to serve as a basis for review and decision. It is reported that Mrs. Scott was originally residing in Tianjin and came to Shanghai for sightseeing last month. The car she was driving was borrowed from Mr. Kasterano, a Westerner at the Yixing Foreign Company. The car was not insured. According to Kasterano, the wrecked car is now beyond repair, and if he can sell it for 50 yuan, it will exceed his expectations, which shows the magnitude of the collision at that time. The deceased Russian policeman Popov was said to have graduated from the Russian Military Academy, was young and handsome, and was serving as a horse patrolman in the French police force, where he was quite diligent. He was only 25 years old and unmarried, and his parents were in Harbin. He resided at number 1288 Route Lafayette in Shanghai. It is believed that he was returning home in the car with friends after a night out when the accident occurred yesterday morning.

Small Hostage is Returned

Because There Was No Milk, the Child Was Entrusted to a Friend's House

The Child's Origin Was Unknown, and the Friend Reported to the Police in Panic

All Persons Involved Were Apprehended One After Another

Transferred to Court Yesterday for Further Interrogation

Gong Yuankui, the owner of Gong Yuanji Hardware Store, a native of Haimen, Zhejiang, lived with his family at 487 Pingliang Road. On the morning of the 24th of this month, at around 10:00 AM, five robbers, four of whom were armed, broke into the Gong's house and ordered them to remain silent. The robbers then drove the male and female masters and servants into one room and locked the door. Then, they ransacked the boxes and chests, looting several pieces of clothing as well as gold watches and foreign currency, but the amount was only worth more than 180 yuan. Unsatisfied with their greed, they saw Gong's beloved son, who was being breastfed by a wet nurse, and kidnapped the child as well. As they fled, they said that if they wanted the "pearl" returned to Hepu, they would have to pay 1,000 yuan to redeem him. Afterwards, Gong reported the robbery to the Yangshupu Police Station and sent a duck-tongue cap and a foreign lock left behind by one of the robbers to the police for investigation. However, Gong's son was not yet one year old, and if he were to starve to death because he was not able to find a wet nurse in a hurry, one of the robbers, named Yang Zhengtin, took the child to the house of his friend Xu Fufu at 3113 Dong Youheng Road to temporarily entrust him there. When Xu asked about the origin of the child, Yang falsely claimed that it was his son and that his wife had gone to the countryside for business, asking Xu to take care of the child for an hour. Xu's wife agreed, and Yang left. Later, Xu learned that Yang had no son and read in the newspaper about the Gong family being robbed and losing their son, so he became suspicious. He immediately reported to the Harbin Police Station, which sent detectives to the scene. Just as Yang returned to Xu's house, he was arrested and taken to the police station along with Xu. Gong Yuankui was summoned to the Harbin Police Station by Detective Lu Gensheng and other police to identify the child, confirming that it was indeed his son, and he was taken home first. The robber Yang then confessed that his accomplices were hiding in room 17 of the Wulin Hotel at 323 Shandong Road. The detectives rushed to the scene and waited until late at night, when the robbers Li Kepeng, Dai Yuwei, Li Xin, and Lu Fucai returned from outside one after another and were arrested. Under interrogation, the robber Lu confessed that the pistols they used were hidden at the home of his mother-in-law, Jiang Yu, at 897 Pingliang Road. The detectives went there overnight and searched the house, finding two pistols and more than 20 bullets. They then went to the house of a Mr. Hu at 259 Pingliang Road and confiscated a pistol, but Hu had already fled. Yesterday morning, the five robbers, including Yang Zhengtin, along with the pistols, bullets, stolen goods, gold watches, and pawn tickets, were sent to the District Court. The police lawyer Zhang Tianyin charged the robbers with kidnapping and robbery. Judge Feng questioned the master, witnesses, and defendants in turn. Since further investigation was still required, he ordered the defendants to be detained and rescheduled the trial.

Extortion Under the Guise of a Kidnapping Case

Zhou Yuquan Was Falsely Accused of Kidnapping

Neighbor Zou Dexin Was Arrested for Extortion

On the 6th of last month, a large gang of bandits arrived in Xiaoqiaotou Town, Wuxi, and in addition to looting, they kidnapped many wealthy households and demanded ransoms. Later, the parties involved learned that the bandit leader was hiding in Shanghai, so they sent Lin Yuanxiang and a Mr. Wu to Shanghai to negotiate the ransom. Lin and the others arrived in Shanghai and stayed at the Xin Su Hotel on Hubei Road. They then reached an agreement with the bandit leader to redeem the kidnapped people for 25,000 yuan. They paid 8,000 yuan in gold at the Hui Dong Hotel in the French Concession, and the remaining 15,000 yuan was scheduled to be paid at the same location on the 18th of this month. When the time came, Lin and the others went there with the money, but they did not meet anyone. Unexpectedly, on the 20th, the bandits were arrested by the French police, and the newspapers reported that the owner of the Xin Su Hotel, Zhou Yuquan (also known as A'gen), a native of Wuxi, was involved. Zhou immediately sent a letter to the newspaper to correct the report. Then, at 5:00 AM on the 22nd, Zhou was still sleeping soundly when Zou Dexin from the Lin'an Hotel at 251 Guangdong Road rushed to Xin Su and woke Zhou up, saying, "The police are going to arrest you. Because of our shared hometown ties, I came to inform you. Quickly come with me to take refuge." Zhou, suddenly hearing this, did not have time to put on his clothes and shoes and followed Zou out. They took a rickshaw to Hongfu Inn at 22 Wuhu Road, where Zou explained the situation in detail, saying, "Because one of the bandits arrested by the police last night implicated you as an accomplice, a detective named Sun Yang at my hotel talked about it, so I came to tell you. If you want to escape punishment, I can help, but it will cost at least 1,000 yuan." Later, after Zou left, Zhou secretly returned to the Xin Su and Shen Jiang (also opened by Zhou) hotels on Hankou Road to ask the employees whether any police officers had come to investigate them. They all replied no. Zhou then realized that Zou had taken the opportunity to extort money after seeing the newspaper report, but he was still worried that he might be implicated, so he went to another place to take refuge temporarily. Zou waited for a long time without hearing back and did not see any sign of Zhou, so he ordered Zhou's maid to return to Wuxi and bring Zhou's wife, Zhang, to Shanghai, telling her about the previous matter. Zhang was deceived and agreed to 1,000 yuan, agreeing to pay the money at the Lao Dingsheng Inn the night before. At this time, Zhou suddenly returned. After Zhang told him about the matter, he immediately reported it to the police station, which sent detectives to Lao Dingsheng. While the two sides were about to hand over the money, the detectives came out and arrested Zou Dexin. Yesterday, he was sent to the District Court, where Judge Zhou interrogated him and ordered the defendant to be detained pending investigation.

Three Punches Result in Death

The Cleaner Was Too Rash

Shen Yusheng Died Tragically

Shen Yusheng, a Ningbo native who was 43 years old, lived in a rural flat in Zhangjiamiao Road, Hongzhen, Zhabei. Shen's family was extremely poor, and he carried vegetables to the Hongkou market to sell every day, earning a meager profit to support his life. On the morning of the 23rd of this month, after Shen finished selling vegetables, he temporarily borrowed a bamboo basket placed there by the Public Works Department to cover his vegetable basket. Li Guijiang, a cleaner with number 13, saw this and mistakenly believed that Shen had stolen it, so he went forward and beat him, three punches all landing on his chest, causing severe injuries. Shen staggered home and fell ill, and died the day before yesterday. His wife, Shen Wang, reported the incident to the Hongkou Police Station, which ordered detectives to arrest the assailant Li Guijiang. Meanwhile, the body was taken to the Forensic Examination Office on Feilun Road. Yesterday morning, Prosecutor Guo Huaipu from the District Court and a forensic doctor arrived at the office to conduct an examination. Seated in the public position, they questioned witnesses Song Shaoyou and Luo Chunfu. According to their statements, they were vegetable vendors in the vegetable market and personally saw Li Guijiang punch Shen fiercely three times in the chest. When questioned, the defendant claimed that he had only slightly pushed Shen's lung area twice and had not punched him. The forensic doctor stated that the deceased had no external wounds and that a detailed autopsy was necessary to clarify the cause of death. Prosecutor Guo then ruled that the cause of Shen Yusheng's death was unclear and that an autopsy should be performed, and the case would be heard again next Monday morning. After the autopsy was completed, the body was handed over to Shen's wife, Shen Wang, who signed a pledge to prepare the coffin.

Policeman Dresses Up as a Beggar

A Policeman Disguises Himself as a Vegetable Seller from the Countryside

Zhang Xiaogou, Who Packaged and Transported Opium, Is Arrested

The Shanghai Nanshi Pujiang Water Patrol Team seized a large quantity of opium, 3,816 taels, and released it through corruption, causing a great uproar, as reported in previous newspapers. It is now learned that the person who packaged and transported the opium was Zhang Xiaogou. This person opened a small cargo business at the Wanyu Wharf in Nanshi (which specializes in receiving stolen goods), and also operated a barge business. The packaging and transportation of opium was contracted by him and his colleague Mr. Wu. Because of these illegitimate side businesses, his income was abundant and his assets were strong. Zhang was very cunning and had many hideouts, making it difficult to find him. He also had many followers, making it difficult to catch him without causing trouble. He was one of the most outstanding villains in society, so the Public Security Bureau had not been able to arrest him. At the same time, after the District Court accepted the case, it researched and concluded that Zhang Xiaogou was responsible for the packaging and transportation, so it repeatedly issued arrest warrants but failed to apprehend him. It then ordered detectives Zhang Chunsen and Xue Bingzhang to arrest him. The detectives did not spare any effort and tried various methods, but after many days, they knew that Zhang Xiaogou was extremely cunning and had great powers, and that hasty arrests would be ineffective. Therefore, in recent days, they changed their strategy. Zhang Chunsen disguised himself as a beggar, and Xue Bingzhang disguised himself as a vegetable seller from the countryside, and went to sleep on the steps of the building around 4:00 AM in the early morning to observe the situation. Zhang Xiaogou, seeing that there had been no uniformed officers wandering around in recent days, thought that he was safe, so he stayed at home the night before. When the sky began to turn white in the east, Zhang thought that it was very inconvenient during the day, so he rushed out. Unexpectedly, a beggar and a villager suddenly got up and grabbed his arms. Zhang still did not know what was happening and shouted loudly, thinking, "Where did these wretched beggars come from, daring to play tricks on me?" After the police showed their warrants, Zhang was stunned and had no choice but to surrender obediently and follow them to the station. After reporting to Prosecutor Yang, who opened the court for a preliminary hearing, he was ordered to be detained pending instructions.

Declaration of 75 Labor Unions Regarding the Xin Case

Representatives of the Support Association Petitioned the Municipal Government Yesterday

Yesterday, seventy-five labor unions in this city issued a joint declaration regarding the Xin Dingxiang case, stating roughly: "Fellow countrymen across the nation, the French imperialists, wielding unequal treaties as their shield, invade our national sovereignty and slaughter our compatriots. One tragic incident after another is continuously manufactured. They call themselves civilized nations, yet they are as savage and unrestrained as beasts, running rampant in our Chinese territory. Especially with the Xin case, the entire country is filled with indignation and fury. We are neither their slaves, nor chickens, dogs, cattle, or horses, so why must we be slaughtered like this? Our national rights are being eroded by them like silkworms, and our people are treated worse than weeds. Anyone with a heart must feel sorrow and anger. Their staging of this Xin case tragedy further exposes their inhuman brutality. Regardless of how formidable their guns and cannons may be, we know that we have the fierce spirit of the people to engage in a desperate struggle with them. We will not rest until we achieve a fundamental and comprehensive solution. Our associations vow to be a strong backing. We hope that all fellow countrymen will rise up together, join our battle lines, and fight them to the death. We would rather be shattered jade than preserved tile. We hope everyone will rise up and plan together. This is our declaration." (The following omitted)

Zhahua Vessel Collides with Coal Barge

Zhiba Sha Caused the Accident Inadvertently

Coal Sinks to the Bottom of the River, People Fall into the Water

Zhou Baolin, a barge owner from Pudong, along with his foreman Miao Gen, were hired by Yongcheng Coal Company on the banks of the Suzhou Creek in northern Shanghai on the day before yesterday at 12:25 PM. At the Coal Industry Company wharf of Pudong, twenty-five tons of white coal were loaded, and the boat was docked on the wharf side. Four people on the boat were having lunch together, unexpectedly, the Zhiba Sha ship of the Dutch Zhahua Company entered the port and, when turning around in that river area, inadvertently collided with the barge. Instantly, the boat capsized, the bottom facing the sky, and the coal cargo was all sunk to the bottom of the river. Zhou and the other three also fell into the water, frantically calling for help. Neighboring boat owners rushed to rescue them ashore, narrowly escaping death. Afterwards, upon inspection, the barge's hull was found to have been shattered. The amount of loss is countless and will be negotiated with the company.

Case of the Violent Death of a Chinese Constable's Daughter-in-Law

Defendant Objects to the Examination

Father and Three Sons Detained Pending Further Interrogation

Li Zhangshi, the eldest daughter-in-law of Li Qingfu, Chinese constable No. 615 of the Gordon Road police station, suddenly died at 4:00 AM on August 28th. Her family, believing she died of acute fever, did not report it to the police station and hastily put her in a coffin and placed it at the Yangzhou Guild Hall in Zhabei. The next day, the Gordon Road police station received an external letter regarding the matter, stating that Li Zhangshi's death was not due to fever but was strangled to death by her parents-in-law, husband, and others. The police chief, considering it a homicide case, ordered detectives to transport the coffin to the autopsy room. The forensic doctor of the Special District Court, after examination, determined that it was indeed strangulation. The police then, based on the forensic doctor's report, filed a joint homicide lawsuit against Li Qingfu, his wife Li Chenshi, his eldest son Li Yulong, and his second son Li Yukun. After repeated court hearings, the defendant Li Chenshi also confessed that her daughter-in-law did not die of fever but hanged herself. Judge Wu then postponed the case and investigated all the evidence. Unexpectedly, Li Chenshi also died of illness. Therefore, it was postponed until yesterday morning before continuing the hearing. However, the police lawyer Wang Huitang again requested a postponement. The reason is that after the incident where the forensic doctor of the Special District Court and the Western doctor of the Municipal Council examined the same body and had different reports, the defendants in this case have found an excuse. Recently, the defendants' defense lawyer submitted a statement to the court, arguing that the forensic doctor's determination that Li Zhangshi's death was due to strangulation was not without error. Therefore, the police lawyer argued that the preliminary issue in this case is still the cause of the deceased's death, whether it was strangulation or suicide, and further investigation is still needed, so a further postponement is necessary. Judge Wu then immediately asked where the deceased's coffin was currently located. Lawyer Wang said that the coffin is still temporarily placed in the Yangzhou Guild Hall. Judge Wu then examined in detail a strip of murder belt submitted in the case, and ordered a postponement. Li Qingfu and his sons were remanded, awaiting further interrogation of witnesses.

Woman's Divorce Case Awaiting Judgment

Gong Wushi, a woman from Suzhou, is currently 29 years old and lives at No. 2, Lane 123, Jingxiu Road, Old West Gate. She was married to Gong Qiusheng (also known as Gong Qiulin), who runs a tofu shop, as his second wife by her parents in September of the 15th year of the Republic (1926). After the marriage, they lived together in the Wansheng Bridge shop. However, Gong Qiusheng became addicted to opium. In March of the following year, he transferred the shop to someone else, leaving only a small room behind the shop for residence. Since then, Gong has been wandering outside, neglecting the family's livelihood. The woman was forced to eat at her mother's house. In October of that year, she gave birth to a daughter. After searching everywhere, her husband was nowhere to be found. Later, the woman learned that her husband often went to the home of Gong's ex-wife's mother at No. 28, Haichao Temple Road, and that Gong Jiansheng (Gong Qiusheng's father) was also often seen there. The woman went to rely on them, but her husband never once came. Before long, she was rejected and returned to her mother's home to live temporarily. For the past three years, the woman has felt that the future is long and the future is bleak. Therefore, she hired lawyers Xue Jiaqi and Wang Zuxun to file a divorce lawsuit with the District Court, with the reason being abandonment for more than three years, which can be said to be the end of affection. The plaintiff's mother's family has many mouths to feed. In this autumn when rice is as expensive as pearls, life is difficult, and the plaintiff really has no choice but to rely on her family. She requests to be granted a divorce. The defendant Gong Qiusheng also hired lawyer Liu Xiang to file a defense and counterclaim for cohabitation. The case has been heard several times, but the defendant has not appeared in court. The case has been suspended without a conclusion. Yesterday morning, Judge Zhang Jinjian continued the hearing. Both parties appeared in court with their lawyers. First, the plaintiff Gong Wushi briefly stated the previous situation and said that all her clothes and ornaments have been pawned and exhausted. She requests to be granted a divorce. Next, the defendant Gong Qiusheng testified that he is 33 years old, a businessman, currently living at No. 28, Haichao Temple Road, with his ancestral home in Nanhui. There are still grandparents in his family. On September 26th of the 15th year of the Republic (1926), he remarried the plaintiff as his second wife. He then went to Nanjing to work in a lamp factory with a monthly salary of 30 yuan, bringing home 20 or 15 yuan for household expenses each month. Last year, the plaintiff returned to her mother's home. I went to pick her up, but the plaintiff refused. This time the plaintiff filed a lawsuit. I was sick in Nanjing and my father informed me in a letter. The shop I opened earlier has already closed. My broker has difficulty marrying a wife, so I cannot agree to the plaintiff's request for divorce and request the dismissal of the plaintiff's lawsuit and a judgment of cohabitation. The judge, having heard the testimony, said to the lawyers of both parties, "Is there any hope of reconciliation in this case?" Lawyer Xue said that the plaintiff currently has three conditions. If the defendant can agree, the plaintiff is willing to cohabit: (1) The plaintiff's living expenses for the past three years, which were borrowed from others, totaling 640 yuan, should be reimbursed by the defendant in full; (2) The house where they live should be rented by the defendant; (3) The defendant should pay the plaintiff 30 yuan per month for living expenses. The judge questioned the defendant, who said he was unable to bear the burden. Therefore, reconciliation was unsuccessful. He then invited Prosecutor Wu to the court to express his opinion. The judge ordered the debate to begin. The lawyers of both parties argued for a long time and determined that the debate was over, scheduling the judgment for 1:00 PM on the 29th.

Cantonese Woman's Divorce Case Attempted Reconciliation

Xili Hanxian, a Cantonese woman, recently hired lawyer Wu Chengyu to sue her husband Xili Zhonghu in the District Court for three reasons: failure to provide living expenses, refusal to cohabit, and taking a concubine. Recently, he took a concubine named Yang, abandoned me, and does not support me. That's why I'm asking for 8,000 yuan in alimony and the return of the dowry worth 1,800 yuan. The defendant Xili Zhonghu testified that he is 29 years old, from Nanhai, Guangdong, and lives on Disiwei Road. He is currently a clerk at a foreign company with a monthly salary of 50 yuan. The plaintiff does not abide by the virtues of a wife, does not care for the household on weekdays, and often goes out under various pretexts, with unknown whereabouts. I have advised her in vain. I do not want a divorce. Moreover, the wedding expenses were more than 2,000 yuan when I married her. The judge, having heard the testimony, ordered the lawyers of both parties to go out for reconciliation. Blind Man Killed by Car

At 9:50 PM on the 24th of this month, an unnamed blind man of about 40 years old was walking on the Xixin Bridge street on Avenue Edward VII when Tram No. 201 of the French Electric Tramway Company, driven by the driver, came along. He ordered photos to be taken and instructed Tongren Fuyuantang to provide a coffin for burial, awaiting identification by relatives. Zhang and Li's Wedding Record

Zhang Deyi's son, Dr. Zhang Yuncha, a trauma specialist, is currently a medical officer in the Wu'an Bureau. On the 16th of this month, he held a wedding ceremony with Ms. Li Guangyu, a high-achieving student of Wuben Girls' School. The couple's wedding photo is rounded off.

Two Bandits Each Sentenced to One Year

Two bandits, Yang Bin and Jie Jifa, impersonated detectives in the French Concession the day before yesterday. On the pretext of checking pedestrians, they took the opportunity to rob. They successively robbed Qi Haiqiao, Weng Tucai, and Hu Agui of silver dollars, totaling more than 200 yuan, which they divided and spent. They were detected by Xu Fuqing, head of the regular detectives of the French police, Tao Desheng, deputy head of the detectives, and Wang Maoliu, the contract detective. Yang and Jie were arrested, and only a small amount of the stolen money was found. They were taken to the police station. Yesterday, they were sent to the French Public Concession Court for investigation. The plaintiff complained about the robbery. Questioned Yang and Jie confessed that they had acted as detectives and robbed. Chinese and Western officials sentenced the two defendants to one year in the Western prison each. After the expiration of the term, they will be expelled from the concession forever.

Fire Compensation Ordered with 10% Fine

At No. 14, Tongkang Lane, Mintini Yin Road, French Concession, the house of Mrs. Ding Gao caught fire twice this month, and in the second fire, a four-month-old girl was burned to death. The details have been recorded in previous newspapers. Yesterday, the police brought Ding Gao to the French Public Concession Court for investigation. First, the police chief reported the situation of the two fires in the defendant's house and found that the defendant's house had fire insurance of 2,000 taels, requesting an investigation. Gao confessed that her husband was operating on a foreign ship, so he was not at home. The women are sisters and married to the same husband. The burned girl was born to the woman's younger sister. As for the cause of the fire, it was caused by a fox spirit, which often suddenly turned into an old man with white hair, or a dog or a cat, appearing and disappearing unpredictably, making a lot of noise. The two fires were both in the empty room upstairs. The Chinese and Western officials ordered the defendant to pay compensation and a fine of 10% as a warning.

Weather Report

The Xujiahui Observatory's weather forecast at 4:30 PM yesterday said: The weather is clear and cold, there is fog in the Yangtze River basin, the wind in Shandong and along the coast of the country is non-directional, and there is a northeast wind in the Taiwan Strait. Also, the highest temperature in this city in the 24 hours before 3:00 PM yesterday was 63.5 and the lowest was 31.8. On the same day last year, the highest was 57.0 and the lowest was 27.5.

Letter

To the Editor, I read in your newspaper yesterday a news item about a Guangdong man named Liang Jintang who defrauded people. The name of the Guangdong man happens to match mine, which has caused dozens of my relatives and friends to come and inquire about the truth. There must be many others who have seen the report and mistakenly thought that it involved me. I kindly ask your newspaper to use its influence and include a statement in the "Letters to the Editor" column as soon as possible, stating that the Guangdong man named Liang Jintang in the above news item is not the Guangdong man named Liang Jintang who currently lives at No. 5, Xiangjing Lane, Chuan Highway, Zhabei, so as to avoid misunderstandings. Respectfully, Liang Jintang, November 26, 1920.
