Free Talk

Laugh It Off

— Sea Guest

Mother (to her daughter): Child, how can you be so rude and dare to complain about your father? You really have no respect for your elders.

Daughter: I'm just straightforward, that's how I've always been.

Mother: Look at how I treat him. I'm his equal, but I never dare to offend him.

Daughter: That's because you took a fancy to him back then and married him. You can't complain even if you suffer. I didn't take a fancy to him.

Female A: Three years ago, Mr. C proposed to me. I rejected him. He was very sad and said that his death day had arrived.

Female B: He didn't die, because he proposed to me last night, and I've agreed.

Female A: Then perhaps he's changed in these three years. A living dead man, perhaps.

Diner (to waiter): I've been dining here every day for the past half month, and I'll have to keep eating here. I find it troublesome to tip you every day. I think I'll give you a lump sum at the end of each month.

Waiter: Thank you, sir. But please give me the tips for the second half of this month and next month in advance.

Diner: Huh. That's strange. Why are you in such a hurry?

Waiter: Because I've already resigned from my boss today and won't be working here tomorrow.

A: My uncle made a fortune in the kerosene business. He has a lot of money in hand.

B: How extravagant is he?

A: When starting the stove every day, just to start one fire, he uses a whole case of kerosene.

The Grand Funeral of Mr. Yuan by Ji Baoshan

— Sun Chucheng

Mr. Yuan Guanlan passed away on August 29th of this year. The sorrow and condolences from all circles have been recorded in this newspaper on November 23rd. Mr. Yuan's public funeral was held in the west of Baoshan County by various circles in Baoshan. I was a close friend of Mr. Yuan, despite the age difference. I received the notice in Shanghai the other day, but because I was on official duty in the capital and had not returned, I was unable to attend the memorial service. Therefore, on this day, I specially accompanied Mr. Huang Renzhi to Baoshan to pay our respects and fulfill our friendship. I have recorded the trivial details of what I saw below.

On this day, Mr. Yuan's coffin departed from Yongxi Hall of the Shaoxing Guild Hall outside the West Gate of Shanghai. It was transported by horse-drawn carriage to Qiujiang Road in Zhabei. Then, it was transferred to a motor vehicle of the China Moving Company to be transported to the Baoshan Public Sports Field. Friends and relatives from Shanghai who came to see off the funeral procession returned after reaching the train station. Those who went to Baoshan took the train to Wusong and were picked up by public buses to the south gate of Baoshan. A bright tile shed was specially built inside the sports field, and a white archway was erected high at the entrance. A square table was set up inside the shed, with incense stands and sacrificial offerings. When the coffin arrived at the field, it was moved to the center of the field and transferred to a wooden coffin. At that time, representatives from all circles in Baoshan had gathered at the field and held a public memorial service. Pu Xieying presided over the ceremony, and Wu Zigang was the master of ceremonies. The ceremony was very simple. (1) Offer incense and bow. (2) Offer wine and bow. (3) All participants bow three times. At half-past one, the procession departed from the sports field. In addition to the elephant pavilion and the inscription pavilion, there was the military band of the Hui'er Orphanage, as well as students from various schools and representatives from all circles. They all wore black gauze armbands, paper flowers on their chests, and held long incense sticks, proceeding one after another through Jiaotai Gate. There was a roadside memorial service at the intersection, presided over by Wu Shiqiao. Heading north to the Drum Tower, there was another roadside memorial service, presided over by Wang Zouyun. Turning west to the front of the county school, a white cloth banner with the four characters "门墙洒泪" [tears shed at the door of the school] was hung. Zhao Xudong led the faculty and staff in this roadside memorial service. This school was founded by Mr. Yuan himself thirty years ago. Before entering the normal school, there was another roadside memorial service. Zhu Jiaji, the principal of the school, led all the faculty and staff in the joint memorial service. Outside the West Gate, at the cemetery, behind Qin Yu Villa, a cloth awning was specially erected above the tomb. The tomb was built with terrazzo, painted red inside, and inscribed with Mr. Yuan's birth and death dates and times. A tombstone was laid below. The coffin was painted entirely in vermillion red, and there were golden characters at the head that read: "The coffin of the late Mr. Yuan, named Xitao, with the posthumous title of Hongyi, a citizen of the Republic of China." Mr. Yuan's younger brothers, Mr. Xi Lian and Mr. Xi Luo, wore white clothes and led the entire family, men and women, to surround the tomb. When the coffin was lowered into the grave, the sound of wailing was unbearable. A sacrificial altar was then set up, and friends and relatives holding the ropes surrounded the tomb once before retreating to perform the ceremony. Then the tomb was sealed. Baoshan is located in a remote coastal area. Although it is a county town, the population is not large. On this day, people came from all directions, creating a scene of ten thousand people empty alleys. Mr. Yuan's old residence, which was located inside the South Gate, was already dilapidated. When the ceremonial guard passed by, the villagers all pointed to the house, recalling the circumstances of Mr. Yuan's birth. The distance from the public sports field, around the southwest city, to the cemetery was several miles. Professor Pan Guangdan of Guanghua University, because he injured his foot jumping high while studying at Tsinghua School, had one leg amputated. He walked with wooden crutches. He also followed the funeral procession on this day. I walked alongside him, and the onlookers all pointed and laughed. Mr. Pan nodded in response. His sincerity in admiring Mr. Yuan was even greater than ours. The public funeral ended at three o'clock in the afternoon. Those who held the ropes had been working on an empty stomach without any sign of fatigue, which shows how deeply Mr. Yuan was respected and admired. We then went to the Party Headquarters for a meal. After the meal, we were led by a receptionist to the Public Education Center to see the Yuan Gong Memorial Tower. It was not yet completed. It was about two zhang (approx. 6.6 meters) high, with stone piers underneath. The material was terrazzo, covered by wooden coffins, so the inscriptions could not be seen. It was said that it would be completed next month. Then, we all took public buses to Wusong and took the train back to Shanghai. It was already late at night. I wrote this to express my sorrow.

A Record of the Japanese Club's Banquet

— Ma Mengrong

Mr. Tsuchiya Keizayuu, the president of Mitsui Bank of Japan in Shanghai, has been stationed in Shanghai for fourteen years. He is capable, humble, elegant, and has a deep friendship with the Chinese people. He is also fond of calligraphy and painting. He has spared no effort in promoting anything related to the development of Sino-Japanese art. He contributed greatly to the establishment of the Sino-Japanese Art Society. Recently, he was honorably transferred back to his country by order of the head office. The comrades of the Art Society gave him a farewell banquet at Ziyuan, and each of them created a painting, beautifully bound into a volume, as a farewell gift. Yesterday, he held a return banquet at the Japanese Club, inviting distinguished figures from all walks of life in Shanghai, old friends, and art comrades to bid farewell and introduce the new president, Mr. Hirano Sukeho. About three hundred guests attended, half Chinese and half Japanese, a lively and grand occasion. I recently caught a cold and had not been out for several days. I accepted the invitation and went to the banquet. After entering the banquet hall, Mr. Tsuchiya gave a speech first. President Hirano, Minister Chongguang, and President Zhang Gongquan of the Central Bank also gave speeches. During the banquet, geishas were invited to sing and dance to add to the festivities, which is rarely seen outside. I will record it here as a "Free Talk".

There were a total of five musical performances, including three Japanese-style songs and dances and two Western-style songs and dances. The first was Nagauta Kanijicho, performed by the geishas of the Rokusan Pavilion. There were ten geishas, sitting in two rows. Two of them played the "Man", which sounds like "Hulei", not plucked with fingers, but with ivory combs, sounding like Pipa. Three people beat the small drums. A man played the flute in harmony with them. The tone was harmonious and quiet, probably passed down from our country during the Tang Dynasty. The second was Buyo Tamagawa, also performed by the Rokusan geishas. There were also ten people, three playing the zither, three singing, and four dancing. However, the zither players did not sing, the singers did not dance, and the dancers did not sing either. The dance was light and elegant, like feathers gathering, like dragons swimming, with the ancient style of our country. Later, the number of dancers increased to six, each holding a piece of colored silk, spinning, turning, and flying. The five colors were dazzling, like dragons flying and phoenixes soaring, like brocade, which was quite spectacular. Later, they played Gion Kouta, depicting the autumn scenery of the suburbs. The four dancers were extremely quiet and solemn.

The two Western-style dances were "Yammurisk" and "Hepwahis Dance", performed by the dancers of the Qingniao Dance Hall in Hongkou. They were purely Western-style duets and solo dances. The dancers were young girls who had not yet reached adulthood. The beauty of natural curves was fully revealed. Their skin was beautiful and their bodies were light and graceful. They danced with their hands and feet, as fast as swallows, as light as startled geese, expressing everything vividly. The deep feeling of the flesh aroused applause like thunder. The sailor dance was also spectacular, surpassing the French Montmartre troupe. It was a pity that there were few melodious songs.

The host urged everyone to drink heartily. The geishas also went around pouring wine for the guests. Everyone drank merrily. At the end of the banquet, each person was given a box of cakes and a group photo of the comrades of the Art Society as a souvenir.

By this time, Mr. Yingbin was half drunk, but his excitement was still high. I invited him to go to the Tiansheng Stage to watch the famous amateur actor Zhu Yanan's "Golden Lock Record". Mr. Yingbin agreed. Then I went by car with Hongwei, Manqing, and Jiekang. When we arrived at the stage, Mr. Yingbin said that he felt drunk and had to return to the club. So the four of us went inside to watch the play. Soon, Yanan appeared on the stage. Her voice was melodious and her beauty was natural. Her singing and acting were both excellent, not much inferior to Mei Lanfang, Cheng Yanqiu, and Shuang. The walls were full of couplets, plaques, calligraphy, and paintings, complementing each other. I also wrote a painting of chrysanthemums and mynahs under the moon as a gift, titled: "The beautiful color stands out as the best under the frost, the new sound is like listening in the moon", to express my admiration. After the play, I returned to my residence. It was already midnight. I could not sleep after going to bed, so I wrote this to record it.

Travel Notes in Southeast Asia (84)

— Linghua

The Burmese have many strange customs. I will visit them more. In addition to eating with their hands, they also bathe in clothes, which we consider to be strange. The weather here is hot. We usually take a shower every day. However, in Burma, you must wear pants when you shower. If you are in a special shower room, you can be free. But if you rent a room with people, there is no special shower room. There is only a partition that is one or two feet high. You must wear pants to shower. I find it very difficult. In the past, a big storm arose in Yangon University because the Chinese teachers refused to wear pants when bathing. When entering a country, you should ask about the customs. The power of customs is greater than the law. You must be in awe. Eating with your hands and showering in pants are really strange things in our country, but they are their laws. Burmese men and women can bathe and change pants in the streets. There is a need to wear clothes when bathing. (This paragraph is not easy to explain clearly and requires a lot of incidents, so I have omitted it.) The old Master Zangjing Faxian described the customs of various parts of India. The king ate with his hands. So even the king was like this. India still keeps its customs to this day. So the Buddha also ate with his hands in the past. If those who learn from the Buddha also learn to eat with their hands? Just smile. It reminds me of the customs I got in Jin, there are two sentences: "Fire is burned under the bed, and the roof is cultivated." Those who hear it will be very strange. Try to explain it. In the northern region, the earth kang is burned in winter. Therefore, cooking is also done in the earth kang. At night, they sleep on the kang to keep warm. This is generally the case in the three northeastern provinces. The roof is cultivated by the people on the high mountain slopes, who dig holes in the earth to live in. The soil is hard, and the holes are warm in winter and cold in summer, which is also suitable for hygiene. The top of the hole is a mountain slope, and they still plant grains as usual. I am writing a world customs journal to compare customs from various places to provide research and to dispel narrow-mindedness. A friend from Jin also told me that north of Yanmen Pass, people often wear leather jackets and eat watermelon. This is because the weather is warm and the watermelon ripens after August, when the weather is already cold. So the melons ripen when they are wearing leather jackets. Now that I have come to Southeast Asia, there are only dry and wet seasons. The saying "I don't know the language of spring and autumn" is proven here.

The weather is most hygienic in the rainy season. Because it is slightly cool after the rain, which is about the weather in May in our country. Those who don't know think that Southeast Asia must be very hot in June and July, but in reality, it is not. It is July in the solar calendar, which is June in Shanghai. But I can wear a jacket in Burma because it is after the rain. You can't not cover yourself with a blanket at night. The rainy season is the most hygienic. The rainy season in Burma is from May to October in the solar calendar. The rainy season is the wet season. November to April is the dry season. The dry season is dry and hot, which people fear.

Correspondence from East Asia (23)

— Wu Xiaohou

The current situation of public education for Tokyo citizens. The facilities for public education for Tokyo citizens. Based on my personal experience and observations, they can be divided into the following four categories.

(1) Adult Education. Lectures and seminars in social education in Tokyo are essential elements of adult education facilities. These include the Commercial and Industrial Youth Training Association, citizen lectures, and other training courses.

(1) Citizen Lectures.

Men's Division: 100 students. Twice a week, in the evening. Graduates in six months. (Venue: East Tokyo Municipal Association Hall.)

Women's Division: Same as above.

Research Division: Accepts graduates from the Women's and Men's Divisions. Once a week, during the day. Graduates in five months. (Venue: Same as above.)

Wednesday Division: Once a week, Wednesday evening lectures. (Venue: Same as above.)

Labor Division: Short-term labor lectures at any time. Rotating labor lectures, 22 times a year.

Lecture Materials: Published at any time.

(2) Lecture Meetings.

Commemorative Lectures: Held on National Foundation Day, Emperor's Birthday, Meiji Festival, Meiji Shrine Festival, Hachisaku Earthquake Memorial Day, Autonomy Memorial Day, Peace Memorial Day, etc.

Seasonal Lectures: Held seasonally to prevent traffic accidents, prevent fires, and prevent infectious diseases.

Special Lectures: Held on motherhood and family education, and family management education.

Cultivating Civic Strength: Lectures are held on encouraging diligence and thrift, guiding thought, improving life, and political education.

(3) Commercial and Industrial Youth Training Association.

Training Association: Co-sponsored by the Tokyo Chamber of Commerce and Industry and the Tokyo Industrial Federation. The first and third Sundays of each month.

Research Division: Accepts graduates from the Training Association. Members share and study the realities of commerce and industry, hold occasional conferences and summer mountain climbing trips, etc.

Women's Division: Same purpose. A meeting is held once a month.

(2) Citizen Music and Cultural Life. Music is the only element for urban regulation, life cultivation, and spiritual development. Music is especially necessary for the aesthetic education of citizens. In 1929, a music lecture was established, and famous musicians were hired. Lectures were given at the municipal youth training centers in each district from 6:00 PM to 9:00 PM on Mondays, Tuesdays, and Fridays of each week, and short-term rotating lectures were also given. A music lecture was also established. In addition to the main lectures in July and October, there were lectures in each district every month. Citizens enthusiastically participated, almost to the point of ten thousand people empty streets.

(3) Motion Pictures. Motion pictures are called "Eiga" in Japan, which is what we call movies in China. In addition to the regular children's motion picture show on the 11th and 4th of each month, it is held in the autonomous association halls of each district on the third Sunday of each month. There is also an International Children's Motion Picture Show on each International Day. There is also a Mother's Motion Picture Show for understanding motherhood. There is also a Laborer's Comfort Motion Picture Show, which is also held in each district. In addition, there are also mobile motion pictures, which are shown at various venues about 100 times a year. There is also a special Children's Motion Picture Day, which is held on the first and third Sundays of each month from 9:00 AM to 11:00 AM at the permanent halls designated by the Tokyo Municipality in each district. Viewing fee for educational motion pictures (i.e., admission ticket fee): 10 to 15 sen per child. There is also a Children's Motion Picture Education Investigation Committee, which is an organization for children's motion picture education that prepares consultations and plans facilities for the mayor.

(4) Citizen Sports. For citizen sports and athletic training, there are nine organizations: land training courses, water training courses, nighttime sports practice meetings, visiting coaching associations, citizen sports and athletic meets, citizen water sports meets, sports lectures, gymnastics meets, and swimming supervision.

Commercial News

Abrupt Reversal in the Financial and Gold Markets

Rumors of an Earthquake in a Neighboring Country; Yesterday, the Gold Market Suddenly Reversed, Plunging Five Taels, but the Situation was Uncertain, Falling in the Morning and Rising at Noon; There was a Difference of Five Taels Throughout the Day, and People were Greatly Disturbed; The Foreign Exchange Market also Loosened Slightly; Banks Bought in a Little, but the Posted Prices did not Change; Although the Overseas Silver Market Weakened, there was no Change in Large Bars; Because Yesterday Everyone was Intending to be Bearish, but did not Dare to do so, the Price of Gold Opened Low; The Transactions of Each Firm Varied; Firms like Zhifeng Yong, Fuchang, etc. Sold and then Bought, While Xinheng Shunli, Wanxing, etc. all Bought In; Yongfeng, Hongli, Tongtaichang, Xieyu, etc. all Sold; Later, Rumors Spread of a Slight Earthquake in a Neighboring Country, and the Price Plunged Three Taels; Later, Because Those Who Engaged in Hedging Dumped British Exchange, etc., Firms such as Zhifeng Yong, Fuchang Yuancheng, Yongfuxing Yong, etc. Scrambled to Buy, and the Market Suddenly Turned Bullish; The Price Rose Sharply to Over 97 Taels; Later, the Dalian Syndicate Continued to Buy, so the Market Remained Stable; After that, the Market Atmosphere was Bad, and Rumors Spread, Saying that there had been Another Earthquake in Japan, but in Fact Yuansheng on Behalf of Xinheng Luo and Others Eagerly Sold Their Long Positions, and Hengxing Yongfeng Yuanheng Hongli, etc. Followed Suit, so the Turmoil Arose Suddenly, Turned Downward Sharply, Plunging More than Four Taels, to 92 Taels and 4 Qian, and People were Terrified; However, Because it was Wednesday, the Foreign Exchange Market was Closed.

The Early Market Fell and then Recovered; From the Opening Price of 595 Taels and 8 Qian in the Morning, it Fell 1 Tael and 9 Qian; The Gross Spread was Around 6 Taels, with Some Small Fluctuations; The Price of Silver was 1/8 Lower, because the Price of British Silver Bars had not Changed; The European Market Weakened, but the United States Sold in Small Quantities; Later, Because Fuchang Yongfeng Xieyu, etc. Sold, the Price Fell to 94 Taels and 3 Qian; However, Sumitomo Bought British Gold for December, a Total of 17, and then Banks Traded with Each Other at the Same Price, and Dachen Fuyu Yuanxing Yong, etc. Followed Suit, and the Price Recovered More than 1 Tael; The Initial Posted Price was 95 Taels and 9 Qian, and the Posted Price did not Change, Falling Slightly by a Few Qian; But Huabi Bought Spot Dalian for 1 Tael 2 Qian 8 Fen 625; Korea and Huayi Mutually Traded British Gold for February at 170625; Taiwan Offered Spot Dalian for 1 Tael 2 Qian 8 Fen 625, and Zhifeng Yongfuchang and Hedgers Sold; It was Also Heard that there had been a Slight Earthquake in Japan, and People's Hearts were Shaken, and the Price Gradually Went Down, to Only 93 Taels and 2 Qian at 10:20; Suddenly, Zhifeng Yongfuchang Yu Dafuxing Yong Yuancheng Yong, etc. Scrambled to Buy, and Mitsui, etc. Bought Dalian for November at 1 Tael 2 Qian 8 Fen 375; Wheat Bank Sumitomo, etc. Bought British Gold for January at 170625, and the Price of Gold Suddenly Rose More than 3 Taels, to 97 Taels After 11:00; The Price Fell Back Two Taels Shortly; After 11:30, Zhifeng Yuancheng, etc. Went to the Market to Buy, and the Price Jumped Up More than 1 Tael; At 11:45, it Reached 97 Taels and 4 Qian, but the Sellers were not Idle, and the Price Fell Back 1 Tael Again; The Closing Price at Noon was 6 Taels and 4 Qian, and the Posted Price was Still 631 Taels and 8 Qian, a Difference of More than 36 to 38 Taels; The Closing Price at Noon was 35 Taels.

The Price Fell Back Five Taels in the Afternoon; The Afternoon Market Opened at 95 Taels and 9 Qian, and then Remained Flat; It Fell from 6 Taels and 1 Qian to 5 Taels and 7 Qian, and then Fuchang Sold, and the Indian Exchange Increased by 2 Anna, and Wanxing Bought, and the Price Increased by 1 Tael; At 2:45, it was 6 Taels and 7 Qian, and then it Remained Ordinary; After 3:00, Rumors Suddenly Arose, Saying that Japan had Suffered Another Earthquake, Zhifeng Yong Yufeng Yong Yuanheng Yongfeng Yuanmao Yongcheng Feng Yong Yuda and Yuancheng on Behalf of Xinheng, etc. Tended to Sell, and Xinheng Bought a Large Number of Long Positions, About 2,000; The Market was Terrified, and a Sudden Storm Arose, and the Price Fell More than 4 Taels, to 92 Taels and 4 Qian at 4:00; At This Time, There were Some Fluctuations of 5 or 6 Qian; Soon After, Wan Yu Yuanheng and Retail Investors Took the Opportunity to Buy, so the Price was Pulled Up 1 Tael; At 4:10, it was 3 Taels and 4 Qian, and then it Fell Back to Half a Tael; In Short, the Market Situation was Confused, and the Transactions on the Table were Different; At the Closing at 4:30, it was 592 Taels and 8 Qian, a Sharp Drop of 4 Taels and 9 Qian Compared to the Previous Day; Afterwards, it was Traded at About 93 Taels; The Highest Price During the Day was 97 Taels and 4 Qian, and the Lowest Price was 92 Taels and 4 Qian, a Difference of Five Taels; The Difference in the Posted Price was Slightly Less Than 39 Taels; The Account for November had Been Cleared, December was 99 Taels, January was 96 Taels, the Supplementary Water was 603 Taels, and the Price of Goods in the Morning Market was 95 Taels and 9 Qian, The Afternoon Closing Price was 6 Taels and 3 Qian, and the Afternoon Price was 5 Taels and 9 Qian, the Closing Price was 2 Taels and 7 Qian.
